I don't usually do this but this time I had to.
The first time I went to this place, was to change the tires of my car. I called to make the appointment  asked for prices, chose the tires and all that. When I went to to appointment, I asked about the tires, to be sure the brand was correct. The tires were a different brand, but since the price was similar and the brand was a good one, I said "Well, its fine." I thought it was a misunderstanding. But, Maybe I should have learned from the first time.
The second time, I went for my car's maintenance. Oil chance and everything. Also, they were going to do a "diagnostic". So, the car needed some fixing, where I spent A LOT of money. I was told it had a warranty for 1 year. Some months later, there was a problem around where the car was fixed. I called and said what was wrong, they gave me an appointment for 3 days later. When I went to the appointment, I left the car there. Soon, they called me back and told me that the problem was something else and had to take it somewhere else to be fix, because they couldn't fix what they said was wrong. Well, It was't what they told me it was. On my way to the other mechanic, it got worse, good thing I didn't take the freeway. I called to tell them the problem and they insisted it was what they said, which wasn't. They invented every excuse they could. ( I don't doubt that they didn't even check to see what was wrong. When I took the car there,  it was in the same place I left it, and when I went back for the car and insisted what I was sure was wrong, they didn't even look just started the car and said what was wrong) I supposed when they did the "diagnostic" of the car, they were supposed to help fine the problems it had and try to fix it. That's what I trusted them to do and that's why I took my car for inspection,  not to have it going off in the middle of the road months (not even 3 months)  later from taking it  there. Even if the problem wasn't what they fixed and was something else, they could  have take the time to really take a look and if it was something else, I, of course, would had paid for it.
If you can't cover the warranty of your products and services at least have the decency to say so or even take the time to see what exactly is wrong. Don't make people waste their time and money.<//text>

< review>
I work in the area and I've been here for lunch several times. I cannot even begin to say how happy I am that there is a great Shabu place I can walk to.  My usual is a medium shrimp order with the spicy miso. The broth is sooo good. I've also ordered the Tom yum and curry broths. These taste more like traditional Thai Tom yum soup with all the herbs and lemon grass that make a good Tom yum soup. It has a spicy kick so if you're not into spicy food, skip it. Recently also had the sukiyaki broths but it was too rich and sweet for my taste. The curry base broth is probably my new favorite. It's has the spicy and sweetness of coconut milk.  I love this place and I'm so happy they are open during Covid and following the CDC guidelines.</review>

< user_name>
Duan Dao (DaoHaus)</user_name>
<response>None<//response>< Text>
This place could be so much more if the location was right. Currently this place resides in a part of Downtown Santa Ana redevelopment zone. Very hipster but foot track is non-existent. If this place were in Irvine, Tustin or Costa Mesa it would be booming.

The cuts off meats are amazing as are the vegetable side dishes. The sauces are hugely subjective as I'm more inclined to like the ponzu and gomme sauce from California Shabu Shabu. So you'll have to decide.

I love the atmosphere and decor of the place, very modern with a touch of old Japanese.

Give this place a try I don't think you'll be disappointed.

Edit 9/28/19: we went there today and found that it's under new ownership. But rest assured everything remains the same, good eats with a pleasant atmosphere.<//Text>

<Text>This Japanese style hot pot restaurants is our favorite in OC. Great service, cozy interior, delicious food. The staff is super friendly. The recently revamped menu offers choices of broth, meat types and sides. Beef, kurobuta pork and pork belly slices are tender, buttery and the best all around. Hot pots are placed in front of guests on a communal counter. Ingredients are first dipped in the boiling broth, then in dipping sauce. Vegetables and noodles are also cooked table side. Flavors range from hearty miso to spicy tom yum. Love the sake here! A great dining experience overall.<//Text>< gmap_id>

< review>
Amazing!! This was my first time here and we immediately felt at home. The staff made sure we were sat quickly and offered us advice for the menu. The owner was there too and welcomed us. I also wanted to include how I overheard staff taking care of other customers and it went above and beyond. Seeing staff in a good mood and also seeing the other customers having a good time really set the tone of the place!

For the broth I had the sukiyaki and the 5oz pork belly. The broth was sweeter and stronger than I've had at other shabu but this also meant that the everything was very flavorful after cooking. Often I would have to rely on dipping my food for flavor at other shabu but found this time I could enjoy it straight from the pot! The sauces were also amazing so I could not resist using it a few times. My friend had the shabu shabu broth and couldn't stop praising it during the meal. I can't wait to visit again! üôå< /review>

I went here with my date and we each got our own shabu pot, she got the spicy miso and I got the tonkotsu. Both were solid. The quality and variety of meat available were both superb and the vegetables/sides that come with the meal are standard for shabu.

<user>116341123206486795205< /user>< text>
Instead of sitting in traffic on the 5 freeway,  we decided to stop by downtown Santa Ana for an early dinner.   My husband and I love shabu and tried pretty much every location in Orange County,  so why not try this new location.  I believe it's only beem opened for a couple of months.   Its tucked right next to Yost theater.   Decor is gorgeous with a modern twist.   They have a full bar!!

We wanted to try the basic meat with their shabu shabu basic broth.  So we ordered the large (sumo)  size yojie beef and their large (samurai)  Swai fish (because I've never had swai fish with shabu before.   They have a combo plate that's great for sharing (they do have a reasonable solit entree fee).

The meat was good, I'm glad it didn't come out with frozen slices (always wait for meat to thaw before cooking).  The yojie beef wasn't too fatty.   Swai fish was soft and tender (dont over cook in broth).   Veggies and udon  was basic like any other place.   We opted for brown rice which was I understand can be hard in texture,  but it was a really hard to swallow so i asked for a bowl of white rice,  which was also under cook and a but hard.   Work on the rice texture please!!

Sauces=ponzu it was alright,  a little too much soy sauce for me,  I like it more tangy with a bit more citrus.   Goma  was good, no complaints there.   They also have a third sauce Swisher which is sweet and savory which they let us try for free.   It was too sweet for me.   Each platter comes with only 2 sauces.   Ask to try them before committing.

Service was great we were constantly checked on they made sure we  knew what we were doing.   Overall good food and great experience.</text>

<Text>I think I found my new favorite shabu place. It was so good that I wish I was still eating it right now.

Came here with my sister and bf and made it for happy hour. Loved that they have it until 7 as I usually miss it cause I don't get home til almost 6. We ordered the crispy tofu, pickled veggies and pickled cucumbers. All of the appetizers were really good, I loved that that tofu was really soft and the outside was nice and crispy, and the dipping sauce that it came with was so good too. For the pickled veggies, it reminded me of veggies I would have with my broken rice plate, but it was good and it had a nice pickle to it. The cucumbers here were really good, I like the peanut sauce that was with it, and probably the best I've had before.

For my entree I ordered the Tonkotsu broth with the 5oz prime ribeye meat with double goma sauce. The tonkotsu broth was the best I've had so far and I liked that it wasn't too salty compared to other places or wasn't watered down. The meat was fresh and they give you a good cut of it where it isn't too thin. The goma sauce was spot on delicious. Also I got an add on of the black garlic to add to my soup and its a game charger. It makes the broth taste really good like I don't need how to describe it lol but definitely its a great add on for you broth. Veggies were fresh here and love that they give you the clear and udon noodles and that for your broth they don't charge you extra compared to other places. Also, get the wagyu here, it was like butter and you get a good piece of it too where it's not too thin.

Customer service here is top notch, Cathy and Amanda were great! They were very attentive, and were always checking up on us, making sure we had everything and making sure we were good throughout our meal. Also the owner Lamson, he was great too.

Thanks Kaizen for such a great meal!< /Text><pictures>None< /pictures>< Response>

102376676251798080876<//UserId.>
<Rating>5<//Rating><text>There are a lot of good shabu places in the OC, and my previous favorite spot was Mokkoji......until I tried Kaizen.

I'll be honest and say that the service here IS a bit slower, and I think that is a management issue, but the food here makes up for that. The layout of the restaurant is also kinda weird. There is no "traditional" table seating, as it is only bar seating.

The owner, Lamson, is very inviting and super friendly. And he knows shabu. We ordered the tonkotsu and the tom yum, and Lamson recommended that we added the black garlic oil. That enhanced the soup's flavor greatly. Great recommendation. Even without it, the soup itself was very flavorful. So flavorful that once you cooked the meat in it, you didn't really need any sauce because the soup literally soaked the flavor into the meat. Not a lot of other shabu places have soups this flavorful.

The pot style is also really cool - it's like a metal/clay-looking pot with a traditional handle to carry it. Nice touch. I ordered the angus beef and the quality is just very high. You can tell that the quality of the food here is very high.

After we finished the dinner, we had room for the green tea white chocolate fondue. This is highly recommended. The Melting Pot doesn't offer green tea white chocolate, and Kaizen does it as well as they do.

Lastly, this place closes at 12am on Fridays and Saturdays, while most shabu places are closed by 9 or 10pm on those days. So, you can get shabu late if you're in the area. Highly recommended as the quality of the soup and meats are just above the rest.< /text>< user_name>
John</user_name>

Other oddities include a yogurt green dip for the karage. Definitely don't come expecting a traditional Japanese shabu shabu taste. That said fair overall for the food - nothing outstanding, nothing icky. Stick with the angus or higher grades of beef, which are good. AC made the inside a touch too cold. Pot temperature was a touch too low got faster boiling, so time was spent just waiting for the food to cook. Karage better at Ikkousha ramen, Little Sheep flavors and selection are better, and price of $80 for Kobe+ Combo+karage is just silly vs most other shabu shabu spots for the amount of food (especially beef). Could easily do Tsuruhashi for $80 for two with far tastier bbq beef, too. <review>The wife and I decided we wanted to get some Shabu and wanted to venture into something other than our usual. So we found this place. Wow, am I glad that we did.

This place is tucked in between the Yost and El Mercado Modern Cuisine close to the foodie lovers 4th street market in Downtown Santa Ana. There is PAID private lot parking, right in front of the restaurant. Otherwise there is also FREE street parking surrounding the area.

The ambiance and decor inside is very modern and clean with plenty of bar seating (I suggest sitting in front of the bar). There is a full bar stocked with Japanese Whiskey( YES!), American Whiskey and other liquors. And of course, BEER and SAKE IS SERVED!

I ordered a Japanese old fashion Hibiki Japanese Whiskey and it was taaaaaasty! My wife also decided to get some Sake (Nigori and got two on the house Hot sake's) with some beer! Needless to say, we were feeling pretty good. As for the food, I ordered the Spicy Miso broth with Samurai Sized Angus beef and my my wife decided on Sukiyaki with the Swaifish (white fish). Both orders were superb tasting and plentiful. I was definitely stuffed post meal.

One thing I'd really like to say about this place is the service is ON POINT! Even the owner/general manager was working and introduced himself to us. Please, YOJIE JAPANESE FONDUE SANTA ANA, don't change your service as you become more popular!<//review><pictures>None</pictures><response>None< /response>< gmap_id>
